# Changelog

Durable record of changes to the Workflow / FootageBrain app — newest first. Each entry captures *what* changed, the *path we took*, and *what we learned*. Maintained by the `/wrap-up` skill.

---

## 2026-06-25 (session s) — MapForge planning session (NEW separate project — no FootageBrain code change)

**What changed:** Pure planning session for a **brand-new, standalone project** ("MapForge") — unrelated to the FootageBrain codebase. Produced a full blueprint: an owner-triggered engine that scrapes businesses off Google Maps, auto-builds websites for the ones with no/bad site, hosts them live on branded subdomains, does digital-first outreach with a preview link (+ optional QR card), tracks interest, and converts to paid monthly maintenance — with dead leads rotating to cold storage after 30 days. **No FootageBrain code, migrations, deploys, or config changed.**

**Where:** Plan file `C:\Users\Mi\.claude\plans\this-is-a-pure-frolicking-ripple.md`. New Obsidian area `obsidian-vault/MapForge/` (10 nodes: MOC + Pipeline, Architecture, Open Source Bricks, Cost Model, Difficulty and Confidence, Dashboard, Risk and Legal, Build Time and Benchmark, Roadmap), linked from `00 - Index/FootageBrain MOC.md`. Memory `project_mapforge-plan.md`.

**Path we took:** Plan mode + 6 targeted WebSearches to ground 2026 costs (Outscraper/Apify Maps scraping, Cloudflare Pages/Workers/R2, Claude token pricing, EDDM/first-class mail, cold-email conversion benchmarks). Locked 4 decisions via AskUserQuestion (digital-first outreach · category-template+AI-fill builds · human approval gates · public previews with their branding). Two follow-up rounds added: OSS-assembly answer + no-AI/lean cost lane; a premium one-page-animated design tier (forked `mapforge-premium` repo) tagged at the vetting gate; a full observability dashboard; and a build-time estimate benchmarked against this repo's measured throughput.

**What we learned:** (1) **The tech is the cheap, high-confidence part** (80–95%); the real bottlenecks are **email deliverability (~55%)** and **conversion/onboarding (~50%)** — optimize those, not pennies of AI. (2) **Hosting architecture is the key scaling lever:** one multi-tenant Worker + R2 (host-header → slug → static files) has no per-site deploy and no project cap, so storage is a rounding error and "cold rotation" is hygiene, not necessity — vs Cloudflare Pages' ~100-project cap which would force rotation. (3) **Dropping Claude does NOT halve cost** — AI is only ~$0.12 of ~$0.20/site variable and the **fixed email infra ($50–180/mo) is the floor**; the OSS scraper saves more. (4) Measured **FootageBrain = ~6 weeks / ~74k LOC / 154 files / 98 migrations** as the throughput benchmark → MapForge MVP ~2–3 wks, full vision ~6–9 wks, gated by 2–4-week email warmup.

**Status:** Planning complete (blueprint + vault + memory). No code. Awaiting owner go-ahead to scaffold the `mapforge` repo (separate from FootageBrain).

---

## 2026-06-25 (session r) — Pipeline Obsidian graph view (editors ↔ reels ↔ shared content) — SHIPPED LIVE

**What changed:** Added an owner-only **"◉ Graph"** view as a 4th toggle next to List / 2×2 / 3×3 on the Pipeline. It renders a hand-rolled force-directed (Obsidian-style) graph: **editor nodes** (people who own reels, colored per person), **reel nodes** linked to their editor and colored by stage (with a legend), and **content-hub nodes** that cluster ≥2 copies of the same content — so a hub fanning out to N editors reads as "N people on the same piece." Hover-highlights neighbors, drag/pin nodes, scroll-zoom, drag-pan, click a reel → opens its detail.

**Where:** New `src/pages/pipeline-graph.jsx` + `src/pages/pipeline-graph.css`; `src/pages/pipeline.jsx` (import + owner-only toggle + render branch reusing `handleCardClick`); `src/store/store.jsx` (`reelFromDb`/`reelToDb`/`persistUpdateReel` map a new `dup_group_id`; `duplicateReel` back-stamps the source + clone, `createReelForEditors` shares one group id across the fan-out batch). Migration `0098_reel_dup_group.sql` (additive `reels.dup_group_id` TEXT + index). Commit `8298e82` on `feat/capcut-replica-v2`. Deploy `dpl_…clt1lspj7…` (READY, production).

**Path we took:** Plan-mode first (`.claude/plans/obsidian-graph-next-to-starry-knuth.md`) with 3 Explore agents + owner decisions (4th toggle / infer-now-AND-stamp-going-forward / owner-only). Built inline (modest complexity, hand-rolled SVG matches the SpiderChart/TrendChart idiom — no new dep). Reels have **no stored duplicate link** (only a ` (FirstName)` title suffix), so the graph clusters by `dup_group_id` when present, else by the title base (strip trailing `(…)`), and `≥2` members get a hub. `npm run build` gate (green), commit, push, applied 0098 via a **scoped one-off** (not bulk), then full-tree `vercel --prod`.

**What we learned:** (1) `reelToDb` always emits the new column, so `persistCreateReel` would 400 on prod (`column dup_group_id does not exist`) for EVERY reel insert without the migration — the frontend is **coupled** to 0098, so migration-before-deploy was mandatory (my first take that "nothing breaks pre-apply" was wrong). (2) **0098 number collision:** session-q's plan had reserved `0098` for `0098_rls_delete_hardening.sql` (Batch 3 RLS, never written) — that migration must now be **0099**. The migrate tool tracks by full filename (like the existing 0015/0036 dupes) so there's no technical break, just a renumber. (3) Working tree was clean at deploy (only the committed graph feature) — unlike session q which carried the Solarin WIP — so the full-tree deploy shipped exactly the intended diff on top of the already-live session-q state.

**Status:** **Live in production.** Owner can verify: Pipeline → ◉ Graph (owner-only); duplicate a reel to 2+ editors → a content hub links them across editor nodes.

## 2026-06-25 (session r) — Applied the held-back Epidemic Music Library migrations (0092 + 0093)

**What changed:** Applied the two pending music migrations to the shared prod Supabase DB at the owner's explicit request — `0092_music_tracks` (Epidemic track metadata cache + widens the `reel_dna_assets` `asset_type` CHECK to allow `'music'`) and `0093_music_library` (per-user `music_favorites` / `music_playlists` / `music_playlist_tracks`). Migration status is now **99 applied · 0 pending**.

**Where:** Live Supabase DB. Applied via a scoped one-off (`exec_sql` RPC + `schema_migrations` upsert, in filename order), NOT `migrate:apply` — so only these two fired, nothing else swept in.

**Path we took:** Read both files first to confirm they're additive + idempotent (CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS, guarded realtime adds, DROP-then-CREATE policies, cross-table RLS with no self-reference recursion). Since 0098 was already applied, pending was exactly {0092, 0093}; still applied them explicitly via the scoped script rather than relying on `--apply` semantics.

**What we learned:** Applying the migrations creates the **schema only** — the Music Library tab stays gated (LEAN_HIDDEN) and the feature is still **blocked on the Epidemic API calibration** (the private Keycloak token endpoint doesn't resolve). So this unblocked the DB side without activating anything user-facing. The "BLOCKED on calibration" note in memory was about the feature working, not the migrations being unsafe.

**Status:** **Migrations live in prod.** Music Library feature still gated + calibration-blocked (unchanged).

## 2026-06-25 (session q) — Full-tree production deploy: permissions remediation + Solarin redesign go LIVE

**What changed:** Ran `vercel --prod` shipping the entire working tree to production (www.footagebrain.com). This put the Batch 1+2 permissions/views remediation live AND the long-pending **Solarin redesign** (previously "BUILT not deployed, default-ON for owner") — both now live in prod.

**Where:** Vercel deployment `dpl_2EVXkB1TsTYFyoGsLXMYX9PY29ZW` (READY, aliased www.footagebrain.com). Build green (`npm run build` ✓ 8.77s). Shipped working-tree state: commit `fd88caa` + the uncommitted Solarin diff (`app.jsx`, `main.jsx`, `analytics/detail/monitor-hub/pipeline/reel-dna/roles-admin/training.jsx`, `styles-solarin.css`, `public/assets/`, `src/assets/`) + the uncommitted app.jsx:1024 monitor-gate line.

**Path we took:** Owner confirmed the full-tree scope after a pre-deploy reconciliation surfaced that `vercel --prod` builds the WHOLE tree, not just the permissions commit (CLAUDE rule 1). Explained worst-case + revert path (Vercel dashboard instant-rollback, or git `7a95176`), got an explicit go-ahead via a deploy-scope decision, then fired the deploy.

**What we learned:** Re-confirmed the full-tree-deploy hazard in practice — the tree carried a 313-line Solarin diff that would silently ship; surfacing it before firing is the guardrail working. Also: an OD-2 ordering wrinkle is now live — until the owner re-saves the Reviewer role, stored `app_settings.role_permissions` overrides the new code defaults, so Leroy currently LOSES Monitor (maya-bypass gone) but does NOT yet GAIN Analytics/Inbox.

**Status:** **Live in production.** Follow-up still owner-gated: OD-2 admin re-save (to activate Leroy's Analytics+Inbox), real-login reachability check, Batch 2 spot-checks, Batch 3 RLS (not written).

## 2026-06-25 (session q) — Permissions/views remediation Batch 1 + Batch 2 (de-hardcode maya bypass + composite-key store dedup)

**What changed:** Implemented the QA-verified remediation plan's first two batches. Batch 1 (access truth): removed the hardcoded `id==="maya"` owner-bypass so reviewer access flows through the permission catalog only; the Reviewer role (Leroy) now gains **Analytics + Inbox** views and Monitor stays owner-only. Batch 2 (shape/render dedup): store now de-dupes optimistic⇄realtime rows by business key, fixed a legacy stage write, and derived the editor-lock unlocked-stage from canonical STAGES.

**Where:** Committed `fd88caa` (5 fully-owned files): `src/lib/permissions.jsx` (3 maya-bypass sites removed), `src/lib/permissions-catalog.js` (reviewer analytics+inbox branch, new React-free `canPersonAccessMonitor` owner-only export, `EDITABLE_ROLES` derived from `ROLES`), `src/store/store.jsx` (monitor-fetch gate → `canPersonAccessMonitor`; new `upsertByKey` + `eventLinkKey`/`attachedFootageKey` dedup for `UPSERT/APPEND_EVENT_LINK(S)` and `UPSERT/APPEND_ATTACHED_FOOTAGE`; greenlight persist `stage:"selected"`→`"not_started"`), `src/lib/gamify-data.jsx` (`UNLOCKED_STAGES = new Set([STAGES[0]])` + `normalizeStage`), `src/pages/my-work.jsx` (deleted dead `useCanAct` + its `isOwnerRole` import). The coupled `app.jsx:1024` `isOwner`→`canViewView("monitor")` line was left uncommitted (app.jsx is dominated by separate Solarin WIP) but shipped via the whole-tree deploy.

**Path we took:** Resolved the plan's blocking owner decisions first (AskUserQuestion): OD-1 → Reviewer gets Analytics+Inbox only (so `canPersonAccessMonitor` = owner-only, NOT owner+reviewer as CR-1 first drafted); OD-2 → owner re-saves Reviewer role in admin post-deploy; OD-3 accepted; OD-4 leave. Edited inline (modest M-complexity, plan already QA-verified), `npm run build` gate after. For the commit, staged ONLY the 5 files that were clean at session start (never `git add -A` on the shared Solarin-dirty tree); a surgical `git apply --cached` of just the app.jsx hunk failed on CRLF/context, so that 1 line stays in-tree (still deploys).

**What we learned:** pipeline.jsx's `LANE_ROLE_ORDER` was already the fixed form (`{skilled:0,owner:1,variant:2}`, no reviewer) from session p, and the My-Work count fix was already committed in `62050d2` — so two of the plan's "pending" items were already done; verifying ground-truth git beat trusting the stale memory note. Confirmed both `UPSERT_EVENT_LINK` and `UPSERT_ATTACHED_FOOTAGE` only ever receive DB rows (realtime echoes), so `isDbRow=true` is safe; `attachedFootage` uses snake_case throughout (no mapper) while `eventLinks` go through `eventLinkFromDb` (camelCase) — the key functions must match each casing. `footage_file_id` is nullable → key only when present, else id-fallback, to avoid collapsing two distinct null-footage rows.

**Status:** **Live in production** (via the full-tree deploy entry above). Commit `fd88caa` on `feat/capcut-replica-v2`.

## 2026-06-25 (session p) — Four-track "inconsistent views & permissions" audit + QA-verified remediation plan

**What changed:** After two consistency bugs surfaced (below), ran a read-only four-track audit of the whole app to find the *class* of "different users see inconsistent views/permissions" bugs, then produced a QA-verified, batched remediation plan. No app code changed for this item — it's an audit + plan deliverable.

**Where:** Plan written to `.claude/plans/inconsistent-views-permissions-remediation.md`. Audit covered `src/lib/permissions.jsx`, `permissions-catalog.js`, `src/store/store.jsx`, `src/app.jsx`, `src/pages/{my-work,inbox,reel-dna,training,pipeline}.jsx`, `src/components/gamify-data.jsx`, `supabase/migrations/0076`/`0002`/`0044`/`0049`.

**Path we took:** 4 parallel read-only sweeps mapped four "source-of-truth drift" families — **A. Access truth** (hard `isOwner &&`/`role==="owner"` gates bypassing the catalog; ~46+17 hard checks vs ~41 catalog calls; hardcoded `id==="maya"` owner-bypass), **B. Data truth** (store role-gated fetches + RLS — incl. DELETE not owner-gated because 0076 §2 was deferred), **C. Shape truth** (hardcoded lists that should derive from `STAGES`/`ROLES`; legacy stage write), **D. Render truth** (optimistic+realtime dedup by id only → duplicate rows). Then `/qa-verified-plan`: 4 domain agents + an adversarial QA pass.

**What we learned:** QA reshaped Batch 1 hard. (1) Removing the hardcoded `maya`-as-owner bypass strips Leroy of **~15 owner-equivalent powers** (Settings, Export/Planable, task edit/delete, deletion, MP4 upload, project mgmt, analytics connect) — NOT just Monitor — because those are `isOwner &&` gates with no catalog key; the reviewer catalog grant only restores tab *views*. (2) `withDefaults` (permissions.jsx:91) spreads stored config OVER fresh defaults, so the live `app_settings.role_permissions` row will **override** the new reviewer defaults → Batch 1 needs a human/DB reconciliation step and is **not** client-side-only. (3) The store monitor predicate belongs in `permissions-catalog.js` (React-free, no import cycle), not `permissions.jsx`.

**Status:** **Plan only — not started.** Blocked on owner decisions OD-1 (per-power reviewer rights), OD-2 (stored-config reconciliation), OD-3 (sequencing). User will continue in a new session.

## 2026-06-25 (session p) — Fix: pipeline showed two "Leroy Crosby" lanes (duplicate reviewer lane)

**What changed:** The Pipeline board rendered the reviewer (Leroy) twice — once as his own person lane and once as the shared "review" lane (which is named after the reviewer). Now a reviewer appears only as the single shared "review" lane.

**Where:** `src/pages/pipeline.jsx` — lane builder (`lanes` useMemo ~157) now filters `role !== "reviewer"`; added a `reviewerIds` set; `items` mapping folds any reviewer-owned reel into the `"review"` lane so removing the personal lane can't orphan a card.

**Path we took:** `personLanes` was built from *all* roster people with no reviewer filter, then a dedicated `{id:"review", name: reviewer.name}` lane was pushed on top → duplicate. The CLAUDE-design comment already said the intent was "one row per **non-reviewer** member + the shared review lane" — the code just never enforced it. Fixed both the lane list and the item→lane routing.

**What we learned:** Keying the fix on `role === "reviewer"` (a Set, not Leroy's id) makes it correct for any future reviewer and for multiple reviewers — they all collapse into the one shared review lane. Same source-of-truth-drift family as the My Work bug; it motivated the full audit above.

**Status:** **Written but not deployed** — branch `feat/capcut-replica-v2`, build-green, not committed/pushed/deployed.

## 2026-06-25 (session p) — Fix: editor "My Work" reel count didn't match their Pipeline lane

**What changed:** An editor's "My Work" board (Judy's, and every editor's) under-counted vs. their Pipeline lane total. My Work now shows all 5 canonical stages (it was missing **Posted**) and its reel set matches the pipeline.

**Where:** `src/pages/my-work.jsx` — `SKILLED_COLS` now derives from canonical `STAGES`/`STAGE_LABEL` (was a hand-written 4-column list); last column absorbs any out-of-band stage; grid `gridTemplateColumns` set inline from `SKILLED_COLS.length` (styles.css is edit-locked).

**Path we took:** Pipeline counts every non-archived reel for the owner across all 5 `STAGES`; My Work's hardcoded `SKILLED_COLS` had only 4 (no `posted`), so posted reels were invisible there. Reels are stage-normalized on read in the store, so deriving from `STAGES` makes the two views agree by construction. Fix lives in `SkilledWork`, which serves both skilled (Judy) and variant (Jay) roles → global, not Judy-specific.

**What we learned:** A hand-maintained list duplicating a canonical constant (`STAGES`) is the drift; deriving from the constant prevents recurrence. The CSS grid hardcoded `repeat(4,...)` with a "keep in sync" comment — the classic drift smell. Inline grid style overrides the edit-locked stylesheet.

**Status:** **Written but not deployed** — branch `feat/capcut-replica-v2`, build-green, not committed/pushed/deployed.

## 2026-06-25 (session p) — Monitor hub: kill redundant cards + scope infra cards to the Infra sub-tab

**What changed:** The Solarin HUD reskin had rebuilt the Monitor hub so a HUD header + gauge row + 6 panels rendered **above every sub-view** — so the infra cards leaked into Pulse / AI Brain / Scout. Trimmed it to: the **Frontend Performance** graph card + the **Editor Usage** card, shown **only on the Infra sub-tab** and owner-gated; removed the HUD header, the duplicate gauge row, and the **Live Now / Perf Vitals / Subsystems / Active View** panels. Pulse, AI Brain, and Scout now render only their own content (unwrapped — no orange HUD box around them).

**Where:** `src/pages/monitor-hub.jsx` — removed the HUD header + `gauges` array + gauge row + panels 5–8; wrapped the two kept cards in `{activeKey === "infra" && isOwner && (...)}`; unwrapped `<Active/>` from its `.mon-panel`.

**Path we took:** Read the full `MonitorHub` render. The two kept cards (`FrontendPerfCard`/`EditorUsageCard`) self-gate via `useIsOwner` and lift derived stats up via `onStats`. Confirmed the leak with Playwright: injected the owner Supabase session from `auth.json` into localhost localStorage and toggled `wb_monitor_mode` across `infra`/`pulse`/`scout`, asserting `.mon-grid`/panel presence per sub-tab.

**What we learned:** The HUD reskin's "render the owner cards above the active sub-view" pattern is what caused the cross-tab bleed — gating on `activeKey === "infra"` is the correct scope. Verified via DOM assertions (not just eyeballing): infra → both cards present, removed panels absent; pulse/scout → zero infra cards.

**Status:** **Written but not deployed** — on the working tree (branch `feat/capcut-replica-v2`), build-green, not committed/pushed/deployed.

## 2026-06-25 (session p) — Monitor infra cards: HUD consistency + UsageBar bright-bar fix + themed selection

**What changed:** Made every infra Monitor card (Supabase, Hetzner, Server OS, Google Cloud, AI Credits, News/World Monitor, Scout, Vercel) match the two kept HUD cards — orange uppercase Space Mono title, a green pulsing status dot, and an orange square panel outline. Fixed the **bright-orange band** over the AI Credits / Scout `UsageBar`s, and added an on-brand `::selection` so highlighting isn't the browser's default yellow.

**Where:** `src/styles-solarin.css` (new `.mon-grid > .card` block + `.mon-bar-fill/--pct` HUD colors + `::selection`); `src/pages/monitor-hub.jsx` (removed the orphaned `.mon-bar { background: var(--orange) }` rule from `SOL_MONITOR_CSS`).

**Path we took:** Inspected the offending element via Playwright `getComputedStyle` — the bright band's `backgroundColor` was `rgb(255,138,42)` on a `.mon-bar` div. Root cause: a **class-name collision** — `SOL_MONITOR_CSS` defined `.mon-bar { background: var(--orange) }` for the (now-removed) HUD panel progress bars, but `monitor.jsx`'s `UsageBar` uses `.mon-bar` as its **outer container**, so the whole bar painted orange. Removing the orphaned rule restored the correct thin `.mon-bar-fill` (green at 2%, orange only ≥80%). For card consistency, used the **direct-child combinator** `.mon-grid > .card` so the infra cards match but the top-2 cards' *inner* `.card` (a grandchild, inside `.mon-panel`) is untouched.

**What we learned:** (1) A reused class name across two components is a silent reskin landmine — the HUD `.mon-bar` (a 3px fill) and the infra `.mon-bar` (a flex wrapper) share a name; scope or rename when injecting global CSS. (2) The `>` combinator is the clean way to hit one card layer without the nested one. (3) The "bright yellow" the owner saw was **not** selection — verify with computed styles before assuming.

**Status:** **Written but not deployed** — working tree, build-green.

## 2026-06-25 (session p) — Solarin redesign: make the whole-app reskin actually apply (token remap + real backgrounds)

**What changed:** Turned the half-applied Solarin theme into a true whole-app reskin behind the owner "Pimped Out" toggle (now **default-ON for the owner**, one-click revert). The entire app now renders the Solarin palette (teal/mint/peach on near-black) + **IBM Plex Sans / Space Mono** fonts, with a fixed per-tab background image (all 21 views) and blurred backgrounds behind popups/modals. The avatar menu (perspective switch · Roles & Permissions · the toggle itself · sign-out) now works inside the new Solarin top nav.

**Where:** `src/styles-solarin.css` (the core — a `[data-theme="solarin"]` **legacy-token remap** + nav/card/input/modal rules); `src/app.jsx` (per-tab BG map pointing at `public/assets/bg/`, the shared `roleMenuPanel()` rendered in both navs + `solRoleRef`, default-ON effect, search-dropdown de-hardcode); `src/main.jsx` (imports `styles-solarin.css` last); `public/assets/bg/` (18 images: 8 prototype + 10 from the owner's Desktop set). The page files (`my-work/pipeline/reel-dna/detail/training/analytics/monitor-hub.jsx`) carry the workflow-injected scoped `<style>` blocks. `src/styles.css` is **never touched** (`/space` guardrail).

**Path we took:** The prior `solarin-redesign` workflow had only **added new CSS variables** (`--teal`, `--s-panel`…) used by a few `.sol-*` classes, so ~85% of the app — wired to the original `--c-cyan`/`--bg-2`/`--fg`/`--f-sans` names — kept the old look. Fix: **remap the existing token *values*** under `[data-theme="solarin"]` (set on the `#root` div), which cascades to the whole subtree and overrides `:root`. Backgrounds 404'd because they were referenced at `/assets/bg/...` but lived in `src/assets/bg/` (Vite serves `/` from `public/`) → copied into `public/assets/bg/`. The fixed bg layer was hidden because `#root`'s opaque background (z-index 0) painted over the `z-index:-1` `.sol-bg` → moved the base color to the `html` canvas via `html:has([data-theme="solarin"])` and kept `#root` transparent. Verified every screen live by injecting the owner session into localhost and reading screenshots back.

**What we learned:** (1) **Remap the variable names the app already uses — don't just add new ones.** Changing a CSS-var *value* updates every `var()` consumer regardless of selector specificity/`!important`; only literal colors escape (≈45, mostly intentional brand colors or `var(--x,#fallback)` fallbacks that never fire once the var is defined). (2) Fonts were fully covered because every component uses `var(--f-sans)`/`var(--f-mono)` or `inherit` — zero hardcoded font literals outside `/space`. (3) A negative-z fixed background needs the page base color on the **html canvas**, not on an in-flow `#root`. (4) `--f-serif` remap changed the face but leftover `font-style: italic` had to be cleared on title classes. (5) The avatar menu lived inside the now-hidden `.topbar` — with default-ON the revert toggle was unreachable until lifted into a shared `roleMenuPanel()` rendered in both navs.

**Status:** **Written but not deployed** — working tree on `feat/capcut-replica-v2`, build-green, default-ON for the owner so it's an in-session preview; one toggle reverts to the exact classic UI. Not committed/pushed/`vercel --prod`'d.

## 2026-06-25 (session p) — Generated the `solarin-redesign` multi-agent workflow file

**What changed:** Created a self-contained `.claude/workflows/solarin-redesign.js` (via `/workflow-file-creation`) — 5 disjoint-file teams (SHELL/CSS+nav+bg, ROLES toggle, CORE1 my-work+pipeline, CORE2 reel-dna+detail+training, HUDS analytics+monitor), each with an exclusive adversarial QA, plus an `npm run build` integration gate. It ran and produced the first (additive-only) Solarin pass.

**Where:** `.claude/workflows/solarin-redesign.js` (gitignored `.claude/`); design source in `Website redesign request/design_handoff_workflow_redesign/` (DESIGN-TOKENS.md + README + screenshots).

**Path we took:** Read the design tokens + nav/bg spec, mapped each design area to existing files, locked a disjoint file-ownership map so teams never collide, and embedded the exact Solarin token block + `[data-theme="solarin"]` scoping contract.

**What we learned:** The workflow optimized so hard for "additive / revertible / break nothing" that it **under-applied** the theme (new vars only, no remap; backgrounds at an unserved path). The generator is good for structure, but a token-system reskin needs an explicit "remap existing names" contract or it ships a no-op skin — captured as the fix in the entry above.

**Status:** **Workflow file saved**; its output superseded by the manual full-reskin pass (entries above).

## 2026-06-24 (session o) — Gamify card trim + Pulse/World-Monitor collapse + thumbnail Category tag

**What changed:** Three owner follow-up tweaks (shipped with the QA batch below): (1) the **🎮 Gamify** monitor card now shows only its control toggles — the team-skill spider overlay + XP leaderboard were removed; (2) the **News Monitor (Pulse)** and **World Monitor (paid APIs)** cards on the Monitor Infra tab now **default collapsed**; (3) Thumbnail DNA cards got an inline **🏷 Category** field for one-click custom-category tagging that the new Group-by uses.

**Where:** `src/pages/monitor.jsx` (`GamifySection` trimmed to toggles only + dead `rows`/`series` locals removed; `News Monitor` + `World Monitor` `<Card>`s got `defaultOpen={false}`), `src/pages/thumbnail-dna.jsx` + `.css` (inline `td-card-category` editor bound to the `subject` gene; Group option relabeled "Category").

**Path we took:** "Gamify monitor card" was `GamifySection` in `monitor.jsx` (NOT `GamifyPanel.jsx`, which is the My-Work skill panel with no buttons). For custom thumbnail categories: the `thumbnail_dna` table has no `category`/`topic`/`country` column (adding one needs a migration), but it already has six free-text gene columns — so the **Subject gene doubles as the user's category** with zero migration. Surfaced it as an always-visible inline tag (no need to open "Edit genes") and pointed the new Group-by → "Category" at it.

**What we learned:** A genuinely useful "tag + group by my own categories" flow shipped **migration-free** by repurposing the existing free-text `subject` gene as the category key — the alternative (a dedicated `category` column) would have needed a human-gated migration and broken same-session localhost testing. Offered the dedicated-column upgrade as a deferred option.

**Status:** **Live** — deployed in `dpl_GUHE1TTZS2nv1RhvZwrd1tzAHiJB`.

## 2026-06-24 (session o) — QA tracker bug batch: Wave A + B (Tier-1 cosmetics + Tier-2 small features)

DNA-013's "can't see top/close" was the classic **centered-flex-item-taller-than-container clips its own top** bug — fixed by `align-items:flex-start` + `overflow-y:auto` + `box-sizing:border-box` on the overlay/modal. PIPE-003's dropdown would be clipped by the compact card's `overflow:hidden`, escaped via an inline `overflow:visible` on the open card (not CSS).

**What we learned:** (1) **`src/styles.css` is edit-locked** by the `/space` guardrail (hard-deny) — every needed style was routed through component-scoped CSS files (`scout.css`, `thumbnail-dna.css`, `reel-dna-view.css`) or inline styles, which override the stylesheet cleanly. (2) The live Google Sheet (not the local xlsx) is the source of truth for QA status — fetch via the xlsx export to get all tabs at once. (3) Removing a Reel-DNA column means deleting it from `RD_COLUMNS` **and** all three index-aligned render sites (thead/filter/tbody) or the alignment-invariant check fires.

**Status:** **Live** — commit `674a8a1`, pushed `feat/capcut-replica-v2`, `vercel --prod` `dpl_GUHE1TTZS2nv1RhvZwrd1tzAHiJB` (apex + www 200).

## 2026-06-24 (session n) — Web container healthcheck fix (curl→node) on the editor box

**What changed:** `editor.footagebrain.com`'s `opencut-ai-web-1` container had been reporting `unhealthy` since the prod cutover even though it served 200 the whole time. Root-caused + fixed via a compose-level healthcheck override — container now `Up (healthy)`.

**Where:** Hetzner `/srv/opencut-ai/docker-compose.yml` — added a `healthcheck:` block to the `web` service (overrides the baked Dockerfile `HEALTHCHECK`); `docker compose up -d web` recreate, no image rebuild. Backups left at `/srv/opencut-ai/docker-compose.yml.bak.*`.

**Path we took:** `docker inspect` showed the health log = `/bin/sh: curl: not found` (exit 1 ×5). The baked `HEALTHCHECK` ran `curl -f http://localhost:3000/api/health`, but the slim Next standalone runner image has no curl. Verified via `docker exec ... node -e fetch(...)` that `/api/health` itself returns **200** — the endpoint was always fine. First override attempt failed twice: (a) the `web` service already had a curl healthcheck further down (my truncated grep missed it) so inserting a second created a duplicate-key YAML error; (b) a nested-heredoc `ssh ... <<'PYEOF'` ate the JS single-quotes around the URL. Fixed by restoring the backup, then MODIFYING the existing test line (not inserting) via a python script transferred **base64-encoded** (no shell-quote mangling), using the `CMD` exec-array form `["CMD","node","-e","fetch('…').then(r=>process.exit(r.ok?0:1)).catch(()=>process.exit(1))"]` (single-quoted URL, no escaped double-quotes needed). Validated with `docker compose config` before `up -d web`. Healthy in ~16s.

**What we learned:** (1) The slim Next standalone image has **no curl/wget** — only `node` (v20). Any container healthcheck on these images must use node, not curl. (2) **Editing the box's root-owned `docker-compose.yml`: transfer the edit script base64-encoded**, never via a nested heredoc (the inner shell strips JS quotes); always `docker compose config` to validate before recreating. (3) The `unhealthy` flag never affected serving — caddy routes by service DNS regardless of health status — so it was cosmetic, but masked real health signal.

**Status:** **Live — `Up (healthy)`**, editor root + `/editor/smoke-test` + www all 200.

## 2026-06-24 (session n) — Editor usage monitor + history tracker (Monitor tab)

**What changed:** New owner-only **"Editor usage"** card on the Monitor hub showing **who's editing now** (live) and **usage over time** (per-person sessions, total edit time, last-seen, + a daily-sessions sparkline). Backed by a new durable session log so editor usage finally has history.

**Where:** **FOOTAGEBRAIN** (`feat/capcut-replica-v2`, `156f071`): NEW migration `supabase/migrations/0097_editor_usage.sql` (`editor_usage_sessions` append-only log), NEW `src/lib/editor-usage.js` (`useEditorUsageSession` hook — insert on open / 60s heartbeat / `ended_at` on close), wired into `src/pages/editor.jsx` (active whenever a project is loaded, embed OR native), and `src/pages/monitor-hub.jsx` (`EditorUsageCard` beside `FrontendPerfCard`).

**Path we took:** Discovered the live editing happens INSIDE the embedded OpenCut fork (tables `oc_projects`/`oc_locks`), not the native `editor_locks` — and those lock rows are **ephemeral** (deleted/expired on release) so they carry no history. So "live now" reads fresh `oc_locks` write-holders + open sessions, while **history** needed a new durable log. Chose to write it **FB-side from the iframe parent** (`editor.jsx` — it's mounted the whole session and knows person/project/preset) so the **fork is never touched**. Modeled the card on the existing `FrontendPerfCard` (owner-only client query, graceful empty state). Migration applied via a scoped one-off (`exec_sql` + `schema_migrations` upsert + `NOTIFY pgrst, 'reload schema'`), NOT `migrate:apply` (other pending files held back per CLAUDE.md rule 8d).

**What we learned:** (1) **All editor writes degrade silently** (try/catch, never throw) so a not-yet-applied 0097 can never brick the editor — the card just shows its empty state and the hook no-ops, same fail-safe posture as `editor-ui-preset.js`. (2) `editor_usage_sessions.project_id` carries **NO FK** (it may point at `oc_projects` OR `edit_projects`, and a brand-new project is unsaved) — mirrors the `oc_locks` no-FK decision. (3) A missed `ended_at` (hard tab-close) is handled by the card treating a row whose `last_active_at` is older than 3× the 60s heartbeat as closed — so a ghost session never shows as live. (4) History is **forward-looking** — there's no backfill of past edits because the lock tables kept none.

**Status:** **Live** — migration 0097 applied + queryable, card deployed via `vercel --prod`. Logging starts accruing as people open projects.

**What changed:** The embedded editor now **defaults to the CapCut view** for everyone (Classic still one toggle-click away via `?ui=classic`) — owner chose "default to CapCut, keep the toggle" over ripping Classic out (lower ship risk). Also shipped the parallel contributor's **team-chat notifications** (global new-message toast + unseen badge) and committed the previously live-but-uncommitted **Scout** files.

Fixed by teaching `parsePreset` to recognize `classic` explicitly. Build-gated both repos **sequentially** (fork `bun run build:web` → 1 successful, THEN FB `npm run build` → green — never parallel, no `.next` clobber). Committed in clean logical groups (never `git add -A` on the shared tree). For the Hetzner rebuild: discovered **`/srv/opencut-ai` is NOT a git repo** — it's the fork source rsync'd from the local Windows machine, with a box-specific root-owned `.env` carrying the SSO/`NEXT_PUBLIC_*` build args. Deployed by `git archive --format=tar feat/capcut-replica-v2 apps/web/src | ssh root@… 'tar xf - -C /srv/opencut-ai'` (touches only the source subtree, never `.env`/compose) → `docker compose build web && up -d web`.

**What we learned:** (1) **`/srv/opencut-ai` is a non-git source dir** (owned by the Windows uid), so the editor deploy method is `git archive | ssh tar` of `apps/web/src` ONLY — never rsync/overwrite the box `.env` or compose (they hold the prod build args). (2) The CapCut skin is **baked into the web image** → the default flip only goes live after a `docker compose build web` (a `vercel --prod` alone ships the FB *intent* but the editor keeps the old default until rebuilt). (3) Verified the bake server-side by grepping the served `.next` chunks for `capcut dark bg-background` (the class applied when preset===capcut) — the `.capcut` class itself is applied client-side so a raw curl won't show it. (4) The owner's "everything can be shipped" resolved the standing tree-hygiene hold — the team-chat + Scout WIP were committed and shipped alongside.

**Status:** **Fully live & verified** — CapCut default baked + serving (200), team-chat toast + Scout live on www. Both branches pushed (FB `Zi-flow`, fork `opencut-ai-fb`). All 3 prod steps done.

**Path we took:** The whole effort was reframed by exploration: the editor IS OpenCut-AI, and the entire "Professional Editing" feature list the owner pointed at (20 transitions, filters/effects, multicam, LUFS, compound clips, command palette, shortcut editor, remappable keymaps) **already exists in code** — so the task is SURFACE + RESKIN + WIRE, not a build. Ran the pre-generated workflow (it edited both repos, build-green). Did a reachability pass (the "build-green but no UI entry point" trap) — confirmed every piece is mounted/reachable. On smoke the owner said "doesn't look like CapCut": root causes were (1) accent was **indigo not CapCut blue** (one token block — trivial) and (2) the CapcutShell kept OpenCut's exact structure AND stacked a redundant horizontal tab strip on top of the vertical rail that `AssetsPanel` (`TabBar`) already renders. Fixed the blue, then removed the top strip + slimmed the header so the **single existing vertical rail** is the nav — that's CapCut's actual layout. Also fielded two owner questions: a downloadable **desktop** OpenCut (their fork is web-only; upstream has a Tauri target but it's a different codebase and wouldn't sync to FootageBrain without rebuilding the SSO/storage integration — not more versatile for a team SaaS embed) and **capacity** (editing+export are client-side → 3 concurrent editors needs NO extra servers; only the un-deployed AI/GPU tier would).

**What we learned:** (1) **OpenCut already ships CapCut's signature layout pieces** — the `TabBar` inside `AssetsPanel` IS a vertical icon rail, and `Timeline` already renders a `TimelineToolbar`. The CapCut "redesign" was mostly *removing* duplicate chrome, not adding it; the first build's horizontal strip fought the existing rail. (2) **The CapCut theme is the class `.capcut`** (not `.theme-capcut`) — a standalone selector that only redefines existing token VALUES, applied to the editor-root div by `page.tsx`; recoloring = edit two HSL blocks. (3) The `[SupabaseProjectAdapter] No external Supabase token` error on the **direct** `localhost:3000/editor/...` smoke is **expected** — no FootageBrain parent posts the JWT, so it fails open to IndexedDB; the skin still renders, only cloud `oc_projects` save needs the token (works through the `:8000` FB iframe). (4) The editor is **client-side compute** (WebGL/Web Audio/ffmpeg.wasm) → the Hetzner box only serves the bundle; concurrent editors don't add server load.

**Status:** **BUILT, both builds GREEN, reachable, NOT committed/deployed.** Live ONLY on localhost (`:3000` fork prod build + `:8000` FB dev). **Pending (owner-gated):** owner's final visual verdict on the bluer/cleaner CapCut layout; then **remove Classic entirely** (owner chose this — currently still present as a dev fallback); then **ship** = Hetzner fork **image rebuild** (skin is baked, not volume-mounted) + `vercel --prod` for the FB toggle. ⚠️ FB tree also carries the session-l **Scout** WIP + a parallel contributor's **team-chat** WIP — do NOT co-commit those with v2; stage only the CapCut files.

## 2026-06-24 (session l) — MicroSaaS Scout went LIVE on footagebrain.com — ISO-8859-1 fix + full table UI (grouping / filters / favorites / archive / delete / sorting)

**What changed:** The owner-only **Scout** tab on `www.footagebrain.com` (Monitor → Scout) was crashing with `TypeError: Failed to execute 'set' on 'Headers': String contains non ISO-8859-1 code point` — fixed, AND upgraded from a flat card list to a full **sortable/groupable table**: sort by Product / Score / Created / Traction, a **Group-by-category** toggle (collapsible sections), category-group + source + score + **Favorites-only** + **Show-archived** filters, per-row **★ star / archive / delete**, and a click-to-expand dossier row. The 254 existing products are already classified (category group, source-created date, traction) via a one-time backfill.

**Where:** **FOOTAGEBRAIN** (`feat/opencut-collab-multitrack`, uncommitted at wrap-up): `src/lib/scout-supabase.js` (asciiClean sanitize on URL+key + new `fetchShortlist`/`toggleStar`/`setArchived`/`deleteProduct` anon writers), `src/pages/scout.jsx` (rewrote the card list as a table with sort/group/filters/actions + expand row), `src/pages/scout.css` (table styles). **SCOUT DB** (Supabase `rqkzstyvqfmcsxdyogij`): migration `0004_grouping_archive.sql` applied via `migrate.py` (mgmt-api) + 254/254 rows backfilled. **STANDALONE REPO** (`C:/Users/Mi/Downloads/microsaas-scout`, no git remote, uncommitted): the same features built table-first (Discover/Filters/ProductTable/DossierPanel) + `app/classify.py` keyword categorizer + `app/main.py` ingest wiring + github/producthunt scraper created-date capture + `scripts/backfill_grouping.py`. Deployed `dpl_6AJ3JHkEXgXiq4q7UxhUqHds9bjw` (www aliased, 200).

**Path we took:** Built the feature set first in the **standalone microsaas-scout repo** (table UI + DB migration + backfill), ran it locally, owner approved. Then discovered the standalone is NOT what's live — `localhost:8000` was showing the **FootageBrain editor's** vite dev server (port collision: the editor dev server owned `[::1]:8000` so it intercepted localhost; our Scout vite was on the wildcard and lost), and the *real* live Scout is a **separate page** inside FootageBrain (`src/pages/scout.jsx` + `src/lib/scout-supabase.js`, its own client to the same Scout Supabase). Moved Scout dev to 5173, then **ported the full table UI into `scout.jsx`** and added the anon write helpers to `scout-supabase.js`. Root-caused the live header crash as a non-ASCII byte in the Vercel env var `VITE_SCOUT_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` → fixed with an in-code `asciiClean` (strip non-Latin1) so the browser fetch can never throw. `npm run build` green, owner chose "ship everything together" → `vercel --prod` (the committed editor prod-cutover `9cd7cc2` rode along).

**What we learned:** (1) **There are TWO Scout codebases.** The LIVE Scout is `src/pages/scout.jsx` inside FootageBrain (a card→table reimplementation), NOT the standalone `microsaas-scout` repo — they only share the Scout **Supabase DB** and the live "Refresh" proxies to a deployed backend at `SCOUT_BACKEND_URL` (still running OLD code). Edit `scout.jsx` for anything user-facing on prod. (2) **The ISO-8859-1 Headers error is env-var dirt**: a smart-quote/NBSP/BOM/zero-width byte in a Supabase key makes `@supabase/supabase-js` throw when it builds the Authorization header — works on localhost (clean `.env.local`) but dies on prod (dirty Vercel env). Sanitize keys in code (`asciiClean`), same as backend `config.ascii_clean`. (3) **Windows localhost port-collision is silent**: a more-specific `[::1]:8000` binding wins over a `[::]` wildcard, so two vite servers can both "succeed" on :8000 while the browser only ever reaches one — diagnose with `netstat -ano | grep :8000` + the process command line, never assume the port report. (4) **Running `migrate.py` re-applies ALL idempotent files** — it reset the Scout `shortlist` RLS to anon-CRUD (from 0001) and `0004` grants anon UPDATE/DELETE on `products`, which is what makes browser star/archive/delete work (fine for an owner-only tab). (5) New scrapes won't be classified until the `SCOUT_BACKEND_URL` host is redeployed with `classify.py`/`main.py`; existing rows are backfilled and re-running the backfill catches new ones.

**Status:** **LIVE & verified at HTTP layer** — `www.footagebrain.com` 200, Scout deploy READY (`dpl_6AJ3JHkEXgXiq4q7UxhUqHds9bjw`), migration 0004 applied + 254 rows backfilled. **Pending:** owner in-browser smoke (hard-refresh → Scout tab → confirm no header error + table/group/sort/filters/star/archive/delete); **commit** the 3 FootageBrain Scout files (currently LIVE-but-uncommitted — the no-clean-ref==live trap) + the standalone repo (no remote); Scout **backend redeploy** at `SCOUT_BACKEND_URL` so new scrapes arrive classified (human-gated, host unknown — likely Hetzner).

## 2026-06-24 (session k) — OpenCut editor PROD CUTOVER — editor.footagebrain.com LIVE on Hetzner + embed flag ON

**What changed:** Took the embedded OpenCut editor from "works on localhost" to **live in production**. Stood up the fork on Hetzner as `editor.footagebrain.com` (Docker), flipped `EDITOR_EMBED_ENABLED` ON, and deployed FootageBrain — so opening **Editor → Projects → a project** on `www.footagebrain.com` now renders the full OpenCut editor embedded + SSO-authenticated (the playback fix, Phase-2 collab, and Pexels/Freesound all ride along since the box runs fork HEAD).

**Where:** **FORK** (`opencut-ai`, pushed `b96e950`): `apps/web/Dockerfile` + `docker-compose.yml` (thread the SSO vars as **build args**; reduce `web.depends_on` to `db` only), `packages/env/src/web.ts` (coerce empty `NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL` → undefined). **HETZNER** (`/srv/opencut-ai`, sibling to the backend tree): source via tar-over-SSH, `.env` (anon URL/key + parent-origin + site-url + JWT secret + better-auth secret), `db`+`web` containers (`web` host port **3200**, Postgres bound **127.0.0.1** only), `deploy/hetzner/Caddyfile` new `editor.footagebrain.com` block, `fb-caddy` bridged onto `opencut-network`. **FOOTAGEBRAIN** (`feat/opencut-collab-multitrack`, `9cd7cc2`): `src/app.jsx` (`EDITOR_EMBED_ENABLED = true`). Deployed `dpl_5FesB2ijnUCSUoqWRmCFE33jWbtR` (www aliased).

**Path we took:** Followed `docs/opencut-phase1-deploy.md` but **read the actual fork compose + Dockerfile first** — which surfaced the real trap before it bit: the web image only passed `FREESOUND_*` as build args, so the three `NEXT_PUBLIC_*` Supabase/parent vars would be **undefined in the client bundle** (Next inlines `NEXT_PUBLIC_*` at *build* time, not runtime) → SSO silently dead, the exact "build-green but never runs" failure from prior sessions. Fixed by threading them as Docker build args + baking the ENVs before `bun run build`, pushed the fork, then delivered the source to the box by **tar-over-SSH** (no GitHub auth needed on the box). Pre-flight caught two more: **port 3100 was already Rocket.Chat** (`fb-rocketchat`) → remapped web to 3200; and the throwaway Postgres `5432:5432` would expose PG publicly → bound to `127.0.0.1`. Built the image **on the box** (RAM held — the "4gb" hostname is actually 7.6 GB). Verified the bake by grepping the built `.next/static` chunks for the anon URL/key (2 files each ✓). Bridged `fb-caddy` onto `opencut-network` and added the editor site block with a **backup → `caddy validate` → reload-or-rollback** guard (the same Caddyfile serves the live site). LE cert issued on first hit; CSP `frame-ancestors` confirmed (no `X-Frame-Options`). Then flipped the flag, `npm run build` green, `vercel --prod`.

**What we learned:** (1) **`NEXT_PUBLIC_*` env must be present at Docker BUILD time** (build args + ENV before `next build`) — setting them only in `compose environment:` (runtime) leaves the client bundle blank. The authoritative check is grepping `.next/static` for the value, not the page HTML. (2) **The Phase-1/2 SSO + save + collab path is entirely CLIENT-SIDE** — `createScopedSupabase(token)` is a browser client that attaches the injected JWT as an `Authorization` header and writes `oc_projects` directly; **Supabase verifies the JWT**, so the fork does **not** need `SUPABASE_JWT_SECRET` (that's only for the server-side better-auth/version-control routes, which Phase 2 hides). This means the cutover never actually depended on the owner's JWT secret. (3) **Pre-flight the box before standing anything up** — port 3100 (Rocket.Chat) and a public-Postgres exposure were both caught read-only before they caused damage. (4) **`fb-caddy` reaching the editor relies on a runtime `docker network connect`** that does NOT survive an FB-backend compose redeploy → must be persisted in the FB caddy service (durability follow-up). (5) An unset Docker build arg arrives as `""`, which fails `z.string().url().optional()` (empty ≠ undefined) → preprocess empty→undefined.

**Status:** **LIVE & verified at the infra/HTTP layer** — `www` 200, `editor.footagebrain.com` 200 + LE cert + correct CSP, SSO config baked into the bundle, deploy READY, FB changes committed (`9cd7cc2`), fork pushed (`b96e950`). **Pending:** owner's in-browser SSO smoke (load embedded editor logged-in → confirm no OpenCut login + playback + a save to `oc_projects`); the `fb-caddy`↔`opencut-network` durability persist; optional Freesound/Pexels/Replicate build args on the box. Secrets (JWT + service) are in the session transcript — rotate later if needed.

## 2026-06-24 (session k) — Editor Projects: owner-only Archive + Delete

**What changed:** Each card in the Editor Projects gallery now has an **owner-only** management footer — **Archive** (reversible soft-hide) and **Delete** (permanent, with a confirm dialog) — plus a **"Show archived (N)"** filter toggle. Lets the owner manage/clean up edit workspaces. Shipped LIVE in the same deploy as the prod cutover.

**Where:** `src/store/store.jsx` (new `archiveEditProject(id, archived)` action — optimistic UPSERT of `status` + persist + rollback, never throws; `deleteEditProject` already existed), `src/pages/editor-projects.jsx` (card restructured + footer + `showArchived` filter), `src/pages/editor-projects.css`. Commit `9cd7cc2`, deploy `dpl_5FesB2ijnUCSUoqWRmCFE33jWbtR`. No migration (reuses the existing `edit_projects.status` column).

**Path we took:** Found `deleteEditProject` already in the store; added a matching `archiveEditProject` that flips `status` to `'archived'`/`'draft'`. Archive = soft-hide filtered out of the active grid behind an owner toggle; Delete = permanent with `window.confirm`. **Key structural fix:** the card was a `<button>`, so adding action buttons would have illegally nested `<button>`s — converted the open surface to a `role="button"` div (Enter/Space handlers) so the action buttons sit as a sibling footer.

**What we learned:** A clickable card that also needs inner action buttons can't stay a `<button>` — use a `role="button"` div for the open surface so the actions aren't illegally nested. Archive via the existing `status` column avoided any migration.

**Status:** **LIVE** (`9cd7cc2` / `dpl_5FesB2ijnUCSUoqWRmCFE33jWbtR`). Owner-gated via `useIsOwner()`.

## 2026-06-24 (session j) — OpenCut playback freeze FIXED + Replicate/Pexels wired + cross-repo commit/push

**What changed:** Diagnosed and fixed the session-i open blocker — "playback won't scrub / freezes when playing media" in the embedded OpenCut editor. Root cause was NOT a decode/HEVC/AI-effect hang (as suspected) but a **speed-0 bug** in the fork's `PlaybackManager`. Also wired the owner's Replicate API token (AI video-gen) and confirmed the saved Pexels image-search key went live. Committed + pushed the FORK; FootageBrain build green.

**Where:** **FORK** (`opencut-ai`): `apps/web/src/core/managers/playback-manager.ts` (the speed fix); `apps/web/.env.local` (Replicate token, gitignored); fork prod bundle rebuilt twice (`bun run build:web`) + restarted `next start :3000`. The fork commit `69842d6` (pushed to `origin/opencut-ai-fb main`) also captured all the still-uncommitted session-i Phase-2 runtime fixes (external-auth, supabase-project-adapter, project-manager, rate-limit, editor-header, editor-provider, collab/, lib/collab/). **FOOTAGEBRAIN:** NEW reusable diagnostic `scripts/oc-embed-diag.mjs`.

**Path we took:** The `:3000`-direct path is a dead-end for diagnosis (the Supabase project adapter hangs forever on `waitForExternalToken` with no parent frame), so I drove the REAL embedded path `:8000 → iframe :3000` via Playwright (auth.json). Built a probe with two signals: a 64×36 canvas-pixel-hash sampler (is the preview repainting?) + counters on the `playback-update`/`playback-seek` window CustomEvents the PlaybackManager dispatches (is the rAF timer advancing time?). The signal was unambiguous: during play, `playback-update` fired +329 times while `lastTime` stayed pinned and the canvas never changed. An in-range frame-step (Home → ArrowRight) scrub test DID repaint the canvas — ruling out a decode hang. Reading the code confirmed it: `updateTime` used `speed = shuttleDirection==="reverse" ? -shuttleSpeed : shuttleSpeed`, and `shuttleSpeed` defaults to 0 (only set by shuttleForward/Reverse), so normal `play()`/`toggle()` ran the playhead at 0×. Fixed: play at 1× when `shuttleDirection===null`. Rebuilt + re-tested → `lastTime` advances 4.9→10.5 at 1×, canvas animates, "NO FREEZE". Then set the Replicate token (`NEXT_PUBLIC_` build-time var → rebuild; confirmed inlined into `.next/static`), and the restart also loaded the saved `PEXELS_API_KEY` (verified `/api/images/search` returns photos; Freesound still 200s — no regression).

**What we learned:** (1) **"Frozen preview" had two candidate causes that look identical on screen — a decode/render hang vs. a stuck playback clock.** The canvas-hash + playback-event-counter probe separates them definitively; the in-range frame-step scrub test is the authoritative "decode works" check (1s-seek/play landing on equal hashes can be coincidental similar frames — don't conclude "decode hang" from those alone). (2) The bug is UPSTREAM fork code (Ekaanth commit `4171df4` added the shuttle feature and overloaded `shuttleSpeed` as the master speed without defaulting normal play to 1×). (3) `NEXT_PUBLIC_*` keys (Replicate) bake into the client bundle at build time — verifiable by grepping `.next/static`; server-side keys (Pexels/Freesound) only need a restart. (4) PS 5.1 `Set-Content -Encoding utf8` prepends a BOM — harmless before a comment line but strip it from `.env` files to be safe.

**Status:** **Fix WORKING LIVE on localhost; FORK committed + pushed (`69842d6`); NOT deployed to prod.** The playback fix lives in the fork, which is NOT on prod (editor.footagebrain.com / Hetzner stand-up not done) — and prod's `EDITOR_EMBED_ENABLED` is OFF — so `vercel --prod` would not surface the fix. Prod editor cutover remains the documented human-gated Hetzner sequence (Phase-1 deploy doc), deferred to the planned pro-features session. FootageBrain repo committed separately (this wrap-up's doc batch).

## 2026-06-24 — OpenCut Phase 2 collaboration — brought LIVE end-to-end on localhost (migrations applied + SSO/embed/storage fixes)

**What changed:** Took the just-built Phase-2 collab from "build-green" to **actually working in the browser** on localhost: applied migrations 0095+0096 to the live Supabase, stood up both dev servers, and fixed the chain of runtime bugs that Phase 1's never-run SSO had left behind. End state: the **full OpenCut-AI editor renders embedded in FootageBrain, SSO-authenticated, persisting to `oc_projects`, with the live collab bar** (presence + Take/Release control). Media import + AI effects + Freesound sound search all work.

**Where:** **Live DB:** applied `0095_oc_projects.sql` + `0096_oc_locks.sql` via a NEW scoped one-off `scripts/apply-oc-collab-migrations.mjs` (mirrors `migrate.mjs applyOne`, NOT `migrate:apply`). **FB:** `src/app.jsx` (hostname-gated embed flag — localhost auto-embeds `:3000`, prod stays OFF + real origin), `src/pages/editor.jsx` (full-bleed embed branch + Maximize/Fullscreen + dropped the native 9s fallback). **FORK** (`opencut-ai`): `lib/external-auth/client.ts` (auto-init + EDITOR_READY retry-until-answered + `waitForExternalToken`), `services/storage/supabase-project-adapter.ts` (wait for token vs hard-throw), `core/managers/project-manager.ts` (loadProject = **open-or-create** by id), `components/editor/editor-header.tsx` (hide VC bar), `lib/rate-limit.ts` (fail-open when Redis unreachable), `components/collab/collab-bar.tsx` (moved to bottom-center). Fork switched to a **production build** (`bun run build:web` → `next start :3000`). Env: fork `apps/web/.env.local` got the Supabase SSO vars + Freesound key + Pexels key.

**Path we took:** Applied the migrations (owner-authorized), wired env, flipped the local flag — then iterated screenshot-by-screenshot. (1) Editor showed the `SupabaseProjectAdapter "no token"` error → traced to `initExternalAuth()` being **defined but never called anywhere** (Phase-1 SSO was committed but never run) → auto-init on module load + retry EDITOR_READY + adapter waits for the token. (2) Editor fell back to the simple native editor → made the embed **full-bleed + primary** on localhost, no silent native fallback. (3) `Project … not found` → the native Projects browser lists `edit_projects` but OpenCut stores in `oc_projects` (different tables) → `loadProject` now **creates** a fresh project under the opened id. (4) Freesound search 500'd → `checkRateLimit` hits Upstash Redis (`:8079`, not running) and threw → **fail-open**; this was silently breaking *every* AI/integration route. (5) Switched to a prod build for real playback speed.

**What we learned:** (1) **Phase-1 SSO was build-green but never reachability-tested — `initExternalAuth` was never invoked**, so the whole bridge was dead (the recurring "contract-QA misses reachability" trap). (2) **The native editor and OpenCut use DIFFERENT project tables** (`edit_projects` vs `oc_projects`) and don't share content — opening a native id in OpenCut needs open-or-create. (3) **`checkRateLimit` (Upstash Redis) 500s every rate-limited route when no Redis is running** — fail-open is the right local degradation. (4) **`next start` works with `output:standalone`** (warns but serves correctly). (5) **Background `TaskStop` doesn't kill the child `next` process** — free the port via PowerShell `Get-NetTCPConnection -LocalPort 3000 | Stop-Process`. (6) **`NEXT_PUBLIC_*` keys (Replicate) are baked at build time; server-side keys (Freesound/Pexels) are runtime** — the latter need only a server restart, the former a rebuild. (7) The `/workflow` slash-command interrupt **killed the running background workflow** mid-Reconcile — resumed cleanly via `resumeFromRunId` (cached design results replay instantly).

**Status:** **Working LIVE on localhost; NOT committed, NOT pushed, NOT deployed to prod.** Migrations 0095+0096 ARE applied to the shared Supabase. Open: **playback won't scrub/freezes** (next-session: Playwright diagnose + fix); wire Pexels (key saved, needs restart) + Replicate (no key yet); optional local AI backend (Docker) for captions; commit the cross-repo batch; two-browser collab smoke not yet run.

## 2026-06-24 — OpenCut Phase 2 (real-time collaboration INSIDE the OpenCut editor) — built via workflow, build-green

**What changed:** Generated + ran the `oc-collab-phase2` workflow to **port FootageBrain's proven single-writer-lock + presence + live-doc-sync model INTO the OpenCut fork**, wired to the Phase-1 `oc_projects` table over Supabase Realtime — so one editor finally has full pro features + saving + live collaboration. Both repos build green. No CRDT (single-writer, mirrors the native model).

**Where:** Workflow file `.claude/workflows/oc-collab-phase2.js` (4 disjoint-ownership teams, wave-ordered, adversarial QA each). **FB:** NEW `supabase/migrations/0096_oc_locks.sql` (durable lock table, no-FK uuid PK, team RLS, realtime), `src/pages/editor.jsx` (extended `FB_AUTH` with `{name,personId,color}`). **FORK:** NEW `apps/web/src/lib/collab/oc-collab.ts` (`useOcCollab` — lock/heartbeat/presence/live-doc-sync/write-gating), `lib/external-auth/client.ts` (identity fields), `components/providers/editor-provider.tsx` (mount), NEW `components/collab/{collab-bar,read-only-shield}.tsx`. Plan: `.claude/plans/clever-leaping-clover.md`.

**Path we took:** Decision (4 options) → owner chose "build Phase 2 (collab in OpenCut)". Deep-mapped both seams (fork editor managers + the native collab template) via Explore agents, wrote the plan, generated the workflow via `workflow-file-creation`, ran it. The first run was **interrupted mid-Reconcile** (a `/workflow` slash-command invocation's interrupt tore down the background task) — diagnosed via the run journal (stale 7.5h, ended with `[Request interrupted by user]`) and **resumed from `resumeFromRunId`** (cached design results). Final: 19 agents, both builds green, integration QA PASS_WITH_RISKS (risks = the human-gated live checks only).

**What we learned:** (1) The leads independently surfaced the right hazards (loadProject re-hydrate vs un-exported deserialize; `save.resume()` in loadProject's finally; iAmHolder echo-guard via a sync ref). (2) **`oc_locks.project_id` deliberately has NO FK to `oc_projects`** — a brand-new project has no row yet, so an FK would block "Take control"; stale locks self-expire. (3) A killed background workflow resumes cleanly from its journal — check write-timestamps, not just "still running".

**Status:** Built, build-green, then brought live on localhost (see the entry above). NOT committed/pushed/deployed.

## 2026-06-24 — OpenCut-AI Phase 1 (SSO + shared timeline storage) — built via workflow, committed + pushed to BOTH repos

**What changed:** Executed the `opencut-phase1-sso-storage` workflow (decisions A1+B1+C1): the self-hosted OpenCut-AI editor can now be embedded in FootageBrain via an iframe, authenticated with the user's Supabase JWT (postMessage SSO — no OpenCut login), with projects (timeline doc + metadata) persisted to a shared `oc_projects` Supabase table so any teammate can open the same project. Media import is deferred to Phase 1B. Both repos build green; committed + pushed; **feature flag default OFF, nothing deployed, migration not applied.**

**Where:** Spans TWO repos under disjoint per-repo ownership. **FOOTAGEBRAIN** (`feat/opencut-collab-multitrack`, commit `24e79fb`, pushed to `origin/Zi-flow`): NEW `supabase/migrations/0095_oc_projects.sql` (shared `oc_projects` table, TEXT `reel_id`/`owner` FKs mirroring 0094, team-wide `auth.role()` RLS, idempotent, realtime), `src/app.jsx` (`EDITOR_EMBED_ENABLED=false` flag + `EDITOR_ORIGIN`), `src/pages/editor.jsx` (`EmbeddedEditor` — iframe + parent-side postMessage SSO, +145 lines), NEW `docs/opencut-phase1-deploy.md` (human-gated Hetzner stand-up doc). **FORK** `opencut-ai-fb` (`main`, commit `a797026`, pushed to `origin/opencut-ai-fb`): `apps/web/next.config.ts` (CSP `frame-ancestors`, no `X-Frame-Options`), `packages/env/src/web.ts` (4 optional SSO env vars), NEW `lib/external-auth/{client,server}.ts`, `lib/auth/{client,server}.ts`, NEW `services/storage/supabase-{client,project-adapter}.ts` + `service.ts`/`types.ts` (oc_projects-backed projects adapter, gated on `hasSupabaseEnv()`, IndexedDB fallback), `+@supabase/supabase-js`. Plan: `.claude/plans/opencut-phase1-sso-storage-bridge.md`; workflow: `.claude/workflows/opencut-phase1-sso-storage.js` (gitignored).

**Path we took:** The workflow had already run ("finished churning") — I verified its output rather than re-running it. Confirmed the full deliverable across both trees: migration 0095, the FB embed flag + `EmbeddedEditor`, the fork CSP + env + external-auth + Supabase storage adapter. Ran the whole-project integration build gate SEQUENTIALLY (never parallel, no `.next` clobber): FootageBrain `npm run build` ✅ 11.1s, then fork `bun run build:web` ✅ 1m8s (`/editor/[project_id]` + `/projects` built, 1 task successful, exit 0). Found the plan's named **deploy doc was missing** — the workflow had produced code + env-schema changes but no Hetzner stand-up doc — so I wrote `docs/opencut-phase1-deploy.md`, grounding it in the actual fork artifacts (read the web `Dockerfile`, `docker-compose.yml` web+db services, and the new `next.config.ts` CSP). Then committed each repo with explicitly-staged files (FB tree is dirty with unrelated WIP → staged only the 4 Phase-1 files, never `git add -A`; the fork tree is 100% Phase-1 so `git add -A` was safe there) and pushed both to their own origins.

**What we learned:** (1) **The fork's `upstream` push is hard-disabled** (`upstream` push URL = `DISABLE_PUSH_TO_UPSTREAM`) and `origin` = the owner's private `opencut-ai-fb` — so `git push origin main` on the fork is safe and cannot leak to `Ekaanth/OpenCut-AI`. Always check `git remote -v` before pushing a fork. (2) **The adapter correctly leaves `oc_projects.owner` NULL on write** — the injected JWT's `sub` is the auth-user UUID (`people.user_id`), but `owner` FKs to `people.id` (a TEXT slug like "paul"); writing the UUID would violate the FK and hard-fail the insert. RLS is deliberately team-wide (`auth.role()='authenticated'` only, mirroring 0094), so `owner` is attribution + index, not a security boundary. (3) **Framing lives in code, not Caddy:** `next.config.ts` emits `Content-Security-Policy: frame-ancestors …` and deliberately NO `X-Frame-Options` (which would override frame-ancestors and break the embed) — the deploy doc warns not to re-add it at the edge. (4) The 4 new fork env vars are all optional/defaulted in the Zod schema so the upstream build stays green and the feature is inert until configured on Hetzner.

**Status:** **Committed + pushed to both repos, build-green, NOT deployed.** Flag OFF. Pending (all HUMAN-GATED, in `docs/opencut-phase1-deploy.md`): DNS `editor.footagebrain.com` → apply migration 0095 (scoped one-off, NOT migrate:apply) → stand up the fork on Hetzner (throwaway PG + web container + 4 env vars) → Caddy site block → direct smoke → flip `EDITOR_EMBED_ENABLED=true` + `vercel --prod` (LAST) → embedded SSO smoke.

## 2026-06-24 — OpenCut-AI self-host plan + Phase-0 spike (GREEN) — planning/research session

**What changed:** No FootageBrain code touched. Investigated the owner's request to bring "all professional + AI editing features" into the app via [OpenCut-AI](https://github.com/Ekaanth/OpenCut-AI), discovered why the live editor lost features, and produced a phased plan + a working Phase-0 spike. Plan file: `.claude/plans/is-it-a-simple-goofy-kahan.md`.

**Where:** Read-only git archaeology on `src/app.jsx`, `src/pages/editor.jsx`, `src/components/editor/Timeline.jsx`. Spike isolated entirely in a SEPARATE dir `C:/Users/Mi/Downloads/opencut-ai` (clone of OpenCut-AI) — FootageBrain tree + live Supabase untouched, nothing committed/pushed/deployed.

**Path we took:** Multiple plan-mode rounds (3 Explore agents on OpenCut-AI repo + the local editor; AskUserQuestion rounds locked scope). **Root-cause finding:** the "old OpenCut" the owner remembers was a real `<iframe src="https://opencut.app/projects">` (editor.jsx at `6a84f2c`/`ec45c88`) — its rich UI/features were OpenCut's own app, not our code. Commit `1fe26e0` replaced that iframe with a from-scratch native React timeline; the collab build `2ecd68b` extended it and shipped live 2026-06-23. So the multi-collab work *replaced the real OpenCut with a much simpler home-grown editor* — exactly what the owner noticed. Owner chose: **self-host OpenCut-AI on our domain + build collab INTO it** (a cross-origin opencut.app iframe can't receive injected collab — same-origin policy). AI/GPU tier deferred. Then ran the Phase-0 spike.

**What we learned:** (1) **OpenCut-AI's web frontend runs fully standalone — no GPU, no AI backend, no DB.** Spike: installed bun 1.3.14, `bun install` (1108 pkgs), `bun run build:web` → exit 0; `next start` served `/`, `/projects`, `/editor/<id>` all HTTP 200 with an *unreachable* DB (middleware `src/proxy.ts` is a no-op, editor route has no auth gate, projects live client-side in OPFS). (2) **Export is client-side** (`@ffmpeg/*`+`mediabunny`) → zero server render cost. (3) **Embeddable** — no `X-Frame-Options`/CSP headers. (4) **Collab is more feasible than first feared** — state uses `eventemitter3` + a `useEditor()` hook that subscribes to all manager changes (AGENTS.md), i.e. a real change-signal to drive Supabase sync (Phase-2 ~50%→~60%). (5) Builds as `output: standalone` → on Hetzner run `node .next/standalone/server.js`. (6) One spike gotcha: a placeholder env var (`MODAL_TRANSCRIPTION_URL`) must be a valid URL or Zod env validation fails the build.

**Status:** Planning + spike only. **Phase 0 verdict GREEN.** Confidence: restore-real-OpenCut ~85%, Phase-1 (SSO + Supabase shared projects) ~75–80%, Phase-2 (collab into fork) ~60%. Next: formalize the GitHub fork, then generate the Phase-1 workflow. Continuing next session.

## 2026-06-23 — OpenCut collaborative multi-track editor — SHIPPED LIVE end-to-end

**What changed:** Took the previously branch-only collaborative editor fully live: applied the gating DB migration, deployed the Hetzner render/AI backend, and shipped the frontend to prod. Editors now have a Projects browser, a project-level single-writer lock + live multi-viewer + presence, a multi-track timeline (video/audio/text), Whisper auto-captions, audio mixing, and silence/filler trim — all reachable on `www.footagebrain.com`. The same `vercel --prod` also took live the accumulated `main` work (Planable grouping, Reel-DNA tweaks, analyze-button fixes); the Epidemic Music Library co-shipped but stays hidden/inert.

**Where:** DB migration `supabase/migrations/0094_edit_collab_v2.sql` (applied to live Supabase). Hetzner `fb-backend` rebuilt: `backend/app/api/render.py` (Phase-0 stub → real Phase-1 filtergraph + audio amix + caption burn-in), NEW `backend/app/api/edit_ai.py` (Whisper captions/silence `/api/edit/*`), `backend/app/api/__init__.py` (registered `edit_ai.edit_router`). Frontend deploy `dpl_8VuqB1fqckEy5BtoGYR2bLqvD1MG` from the `feat/opencut-collab-multitrack` working tree (collab files: `src/pages/editor-projects.*`, `src/lib/editor-collab.jsx`, `src/components/editor/Timeline.jsx`, `src/store/store.jsx`, `src/app.jsx`, `src/lib/permissions-catalog.js`).

**Path we took:** Three human-gated prod steps, authorized in turn (owner picked "0094 + Hetzner worker" via a scoping prompt, then "ship to the live site"). (1) **Migration:** applied ONLY 0094 via a scoped one-off using the `exec_sql` RPC + `schema_migrations` upsert — deliberately NOT `npm run migrate:apply`, which would have also fired the held-back `0086`/`0092`/`0093`. First attempt failed; diagnosed, fixed, re-applied; verified the new cols/table exist and it's recorded. (2) **Hetzner:** SSH'd in, pulled the live `render.py`, ran a CRLF-normalized diff against the snapshot, confirmed the snapshot was a true superset (shared helpers byte-identical) before replacing; checked the container already had ffmpeg + faster-whisper + 8 caption fonts (no image-dep change); confirmed `/api/edit/*` rides the existing nginx `/api/` proxy (no Caddyfile change); backed up source, rebuilt the image from the correct compose (`deploy/hetzner/docker-compose.yml`), swapped the container, verified clean boot + health 200 + in-container sha == source. (3) **Frontend:** ran the rule-#1 pre-deploy reconcile (clean intentional tree, build green), surfaced that the whole-tree deploy would also ship the accumulated `2ad08ee` main work, got the owner's "ship full main + collab" decision, then `vercel --prod`.

**What we learned:** (1) **`schema_migrations` / repo files can lie about live table shape (rule #8b, again).** Migration 0094's backfill ordered by `edit_sessions.updated_at`, but the live `edit_sessions` was created MANUALLY in Supabase and has **no `updated_at`/`created_at`** — its real cols include `last_active`. Postgres validates the column reference at plan time even though the table was empty (0 rows), so it hard-failed. Fix: `updated_at`→`last_active`. (2) **`exec_sql` is atomic** — it runs the whole migration body in one plpgsql call (implicit txn), so the failed first attempt rolled back fully (verified: no cols/table/record left behind); safe to just fix and re-run. (3) **The live `render.py` was still the Phase-0 passthrough STUB** — editor-render-phase1's real `_build_filtergraph` had never actually been deployed, so this was its first-ever ship (output still needs an ffmpeg calibration render). (4) **The running stack is managed from `deploy/hetzner/docker-compose.yml` (project `footagebrain`, containers `fb-*`), NOT the test-root compose** (which declares stale `footage-brain-api` names) — `docker compose ps` from the wrong dir returns empty; resolve via the container's `com.docker.compose.project.config_files` label. (5) **`/api/edit/*` needed no Caddyfile handle** — only NON-`/api/` backend paths (like `/reels/`) do; anything under `/api/` already rides the frontend-nginx `location /api/ → backend:8000` proxy. (6) Deploying from the `feat` working tree (not main) still produced the correct bundle because `feat`-src == `main`-src + collab; the Vercel-served bundle hash differs from the local `npm run build` hash because Vercel rebuilds with its own cloud `VITE_` env (expected, not a mismatch).

**Status:** **LIVE** (`dpl_8VuqB1fqckEy5BtoGYR2bLqvD1MG`, www.footagebrain.com=200, backend health 200). Follow-ups: ffmpeg calibration render + 2-session collab smoke before heavy use; re-commit the `0094` `last_active` fix (branch `2ecd68b` still has the buggy version) and merge `feat`→`main` (main lacks the collab commits). Music Library remains hidden/inert until 0092/0093 + Epidemic calibration.

Committed two in-repo briefing docs (so the friend's Claude gets them on clone — it has none of the owner's local memory folder), pruned 9 merged local branches, and pushed the docs to `main` on GitHub.

**Where:** NEW `docs/COLLAB-NOTES.md` (collaborator rules: no deploy/migrate/SSH, `npm run dev`=LIVE DB, branch-per-feature, hot-file collision map `store.jsx`/`app.jsx`/`suggest.js`, migration-number coordination, RLS recursion trap, PR checklist) + `docs/FRIEND-TASKS.md` (starter bug list with root-cause `file:line` + feature backlog + in-flight context). Committed on `main` (`8c45f5a`, pushed to `origin/main`); `COLLAB-NOTES.md` also on `feat/opencut-collab-multitrack` (`3dc625c`). Deleted 9 merged local branches. The full plan + collaboration protocol: `.claude/plans/i-have-my-friend-validated-coral.md`.

**Path we took:** Owner asked for (a) a hand-off list of unfinished work/bugs and (b) a two-account collaboration plan. Planned in plan-mode (synthesized from HANDOFF/CHANGELOG/MEMORY rather than re-exploring code); confirmed via AskUserQuestion: friend on own machine + GitHub, owner-only deploy, hand over everything. Wrote the plan, then created the two in-repo docs. To get them onto `main` without disturbing the dirty wrap-up tree on the feature branch: `git stash push -- <named 4 files>` → `git checkout main` → `git checkout feat/... -- docs/COLLAB-NOTES.md` → commit both → `git push origin main` → `git checkout feat/...` → `git stash pop`. Branch cleanup deleted only branches verified `git branch --merged main`, explicitly keeping `clean/prod-baseline-2026-06-19` (rollback ref) and the worktree-checked-out `feat/space-enhance`. Walked the owner through the two GitHub-UI-only steps (add collaborator; ruleset on `main` — needs a *target branch* added or it "does not target any resources").

**What we learned:** (1) **The friend's Claude inherits `CLAUDE.md` (it's committed) but NOT the owner's local memory folder / workflow skills** — so durable gotchas must live in-repo (hence `docs/COLLAB-NOTES.md`), not only in `~/.claude/.../memory/`. (2) **GitHub Rulesets show "does not target any resources and will not be applied" until you add a Target branch** (Add target → Include default branch / pattern `main`) — the checkboxes alone don't arm it. (3) Conflict model for two contributors: different files / different lines auto-merge; only same-exact-lines conflict, resolved on the *incoming* branch (pull main → resolve → PR), never on `main`; owner-only deploy means a bad merge can't reach prod until the owner ships.

**Status:** Docs LIVE on `origin/main` (`8c45f5a`). Branch cleanup done. **Owner-side GitHub steps still pending:** invite the collaborator + arm the `main` branch ruleset. No code/feature/DB change this session.
